C-d: ≜
C-l: λ

C-e: add definition or do one step of evaluation

like, cursor somewhere on next line and do C-e:
I ≜ λx.x

C-S-e: evaluate until normal form, or like at least 1000 steps
C-r: replace names of things you have defined with their definitions

like, cursor on next line, C-r, then C-e or C-S-e:
I I I I foo



Renaming variables to avoid capture counts as one step:
like,
λx.(λy.λx.y) x

There's a buch of definitions in the cheat-slide:
(slide "cheat")


(λf.f) foo

(slide "rules")
------------------------------------------------------------
Syntax:
Exp u ::= x         variable
          λx.u      abstraction
          u1 u2     application
 
Computation rule:
(λx.u1) u2
[u2/x]u1

e.g.
(λa.λb.λc.a c c) foo bar quux
(λb.λc.foo c c) bar quux
(λc.foo c c) quux
foo quux quux
------------------------------------------------------------

(slide "who-needs-booleans")
------------------------------------------------------------
* A boolean just makes a choice!

    true  x y = x
    true ≜ λx.λy.x

asd ≜ λx.asd x
asd :)

asd 
λx.asd x
λx.(λx.asd x) x
λx.(λx.(λx.asd x) x) x
λx.(λx.(λx.(λx.asd x) x) x) x
λx.(λx.(λx.asd x) x) x
λx.(λx.asd x) x
λx.asd x
λx.asd x

true :)
λx.true
λx.λx.λy.x

    false x y = y

false ≜ λx.λy.y
false :)


true then else
(λx.λy.x) then else
(λy.then) else
then

false then else
(λx.λy.y) then else
(λy.y) else
else

* We can define if-then-else!

    ifte bool t e = bool t e

ifte ≜ λbool.λt.λe.bool t e
ifte :)

(slide "who-needs-integers")
------------------------------------------------------------
* A (positive) integer just counts loop iterations!

    two  f x = f (f x)
    2 ≜ λf.λx.f (f x)
2 :)
    one  f x = f x
    1 ≜ λf.λx.f x
1 :)
    zero f x = x
    0 ≜ λf.λx.x
0 :)

* To recover a "normal" integer

    *Church> two (+1-- wait. no. um.
    M-x count-matches I guess

(slide "pred")
------------------------------------------------------------
replace f with something that takes (a, b) to (a + 1, a)
replace x with (0, 0)
0
1
2
3

so like,
(0, 0)
(1, 0)
(2, 1)
(3, 2)
...

then pick the second part of the pair to get previous number
------------------------------------------------------------

pair ≜ λa.λb.λf.f a b
pair :)

pair foo bar
(λa.λb.λf.f a b) foo bar
(λb.λf.f foo b) bar


(λf.f foo bar) (λa.λb.b)
(λa.λb.b) foo bar
(λb.b) bar
bar

fst ≜ λp.p (λa.λb.a)
fst :)

snd ≜ λp.p (λa.λb.b)
snd :)

fst (pair foo bar)
(λp.p (λa.λb.a)) ((λa.λb.λf.f a b) foo bar)
(λa.λb.λf.f a b) foo bar (λa.λb.a)
(λb.λf.f foo b) bar (λa.λb.a)
(λf.f foo bar) (λa.λb.a)
(λa.λb.a) foo bar
(λb.foo) bar
foo

snd (pair foo bar)
(λp.p (λa.λb.b)) ((λa.λb.λf.f a b) foo bar)
(λa.λb.λf.f a b) foo bar (λa.λb.b)
(λb.λf.f foo b) bar (λa.λb.b)
(λf.f foo bar) (λa.λb.b)
(λa.λb.b) foo bar
(λb.b) bar
bar

(λa.λb.a) foo bar
(λb.foo) bar
foo

      v       v       v
(cons 1 (cons 2 (cons 3 nil)))

      ʌ       ʌ       ʌ
      |_______|_______|
              |
           no junk

(slide "foldquote")
------------------------------------------------------------
In fact, a data structure can be faithfully represented by -- is isomorphic to -- its right fold. For example, the entire list processing library, from head and tail to drop and take and even zipWith can be written entirely in terms of foldr.
http://okmij.org/ftp/Haskell/AlgorithmsH1.html#foldl

appendy:

a = (cons 1 (cons 2 nil))
b = (cons 3 (cons 4 nil))

   fold cons b a
=> fold cons b (cons 1 (cons 2 nil))
=>             (cons 1 (cons 2 b))
=>             (cons 1 (cons 2 (cons 3 (cons 4 nil))))

(slide "numfold")
------------------------------------------------------------
so folding a number would be like,

a = S (S (S 0))
b = S (S 0)

plus:
   fold S b a
=> fold S b (S (S (S 0)))
=>          (S (S (S b)))
=>          (S (S (S (S (S 0)))))

mult:
   fold (+ b) 0 a
=> fold (+ b) 0 (S (S (S 0)))
=>              (+ b (+ b (+ b 0)))
=>              (+ (S (S 0)) (+ (S (S 0)) (+ (S (S 0)) 0)))
...
=>              (S (S (S (S (S (S 0))))))
------------------------------------------------------------
